# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully completed the audit and created a comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified **14 critical Go source files** that define and enforce Grafana's three-tier permission model (Viewer/Editor/Admin):

### 1. **Role Definition Layer**
- `pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go` - Defines the RoleType with four constants (None, Viewer, Editor, Admin) and a precedence hierarchy
- `pkg/services/org/model.go` - Maps users to roles through OrgUser model

### 2. **Permission-to-Action Mapping**
- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` - Declares fixed roles and their grants via `DeclareFixedRoles`
- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` - Maps dashboard permissions:
  - **View**: dashboards:read, annotations:read
  - **Edit**: adds dashboards:write, delete, annotations operations
  - **Admin**: adds dashboards.permissions:read/write
- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` - Maps folder permissions with similar hierarchy plus alert and library panel management

### 3. **Permission Guard Middleware**
- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go` - The `Middleware` function enforces permissions via the `Evaluator` interface
- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/evaluator.go` - Defines the `EvalPermission` function that checks actions against scopes

### 4. **Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance**
- `pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go` - Critical `GetInheritedScopes` function retrieves parent folder scopes, enabling hierarchical inheritance
- Scope resolvers (`NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver`, `NewFolderUIDScopeResolver`) convert resource references into permission scopes including parent folder inheritance

### 5. **API and Service Layer**
- `pkg/api

For example, you can use RBAC to:\\n119: \\n120: - Modify existing basic roles: for example, enable an editor to create reports\\n121: - Assign fixed roles to users and teams: for example, grant an engineering team the ability to create data sources\\n122: - Create custom roles: for example, a role that allows users to create and edit dashboards, but not delete them\\n123: \\n124: RBAC roles contain multiple permissions, each of which has an action and a scope:\\n125: \\n126: - **Role:** `fixed:datasources:reader`\\n127:   - **Permission:**\\n128:     - **Action:** `datasources:read`\\n129: ...
